<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Tellurium</h1>			<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
				<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>				<div id="contentSub"></div>
				<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the astronomical device, see <a href="/wiki/Tellurion" title="Tellurion">tellurion</a>.</div>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">chemical element with atomic number 52</div><table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><caption><span style="white-space:nowrap">Tellurium,&#160;&#160;<sub><span style="font-size:smaller;">52</span></sub>Te</span></caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<a href="/wiki/File:Tellurium2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Tellurium2.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Tellurium2.jpg/220px-Tellurium2.jpg" width="220" height="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Tellurium2.jpg/330px-Tellurium2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Tellurium2.jpg/440px-Tellurium2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1170" data-file-height="1170" /></a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background:#cccc99">General properties</th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Pronunciation</th><td>
<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/lj/: &#39;l&#39; in &#39;lute&#39;">lj</span><span title="/ʊər/: &#39;our&#39; in &#39;tour&#39;">ʊər</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span></span>/</a></span></span>&#x20;<wbr />&#8203;<span class="nowrap">(<a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">tə-<span style="font-size:90%">LEWR</span>-ee-əm</i></a>)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Appearance</th><td>
silvery lustrous gray (crystalline),<br />brown-black powder (amorphous)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Standard_atomic_weight" title="Standard atomic weight">Standard atomic weight</a><span style="font-weight:normal;">&#x20;(<i>A</i><sub>r,&#160;standard</sub>)</span></th><td>

<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Infobox_tellurium" title="Template:Infobox tellurium"><span title="View this template">view</span></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Infobox_tellurium" title="Template talk:Infobox tellurium"><span title="Discuss this template">talk</span></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Infobox_tellurium&amp;action=edit"><span title="Edit this template">edit</span></a></li></ul></div>&#x20;|&#x20;<a href="/wiki/List_of_data_references_for_chemical_elements" title="List of data references for chemical elements">references</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Tellurium</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Chemical_element" title="Chemical element">chemical element</a> with symbol&#160;<b>Te</b> and <a href="/wiki/Atomic_number" title="Atomic number">atomic number</a>&#160;52. It is a brittle, mildly toxic, rare, silver-white <a href="/wiki/Metalloid" title="Metalloid">metalloid</a>. Tellurium is chemically related to <a href="/wiki/Selenium" title="Selenium">selenium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sulfur" title="Sulfur">sulfur</a>. It is occasionally found in native form as elemental crystals. Tellurium is far more common in the universe as a whole than on Earth. Its extreme <a href="/wiki/Abundance_of_the_chemical_elements" title="Abundance of the chemical elements">rarity</a> in the Earth's crust, comparable to that of <a href="/wiki/Platinum" title="Platinum">platinum</a>, is due partly to its high atomic number, but also to its formation of a volatile <a href="/wiki/Hydride" title="Hydride">hydride</a> which caused it to be lost to space as a gas during the hot nebular formation of the planet.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Gold_chalcogenides" title="Gold chalcogenides">Tellurium-bearing compounds</a> were first discovered in 1782 in a gold mine in <a href="/wiki/Zlatna" title="Zlatna">Zlatna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> by <a href="/wiki/Austrians" title="Austrians">Austrian</a> <a href="/wiki/Mineralogy" title="Mineralogy">mineralogist</a> <a href="/wiki/Franz-Joseph_M%C3%BCller_von_Reichenstein" title="Franz-Joseph Müller von Reichenstein">Franz-Joseph Müller von Reichenstein</a>, although it was <a href="/wiki/Martin_Heinrich_Klaproth" title="Martin Heinrich Klaproth">Martin Heinrich Klaproth</a> who named the new element in 1798 after the Latin word for "earth", <i>tellus</i>. <a href="/wiki/Gold_telluride" class="mw-redirect" title="Gold telluride">Gold telluride</a> minerals are the most notable natural gold compounds. However, they are not a commercially significant source of tellurium itself, which is normally extracted as a by-product of <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">lead</a> production.
</p><p>Commercially, the primary use of tellurium is copper and steel <a href="/wiki/Alloy" title="Alloy">alloys</a>, where it improves <a href="/wiki/Machinability" title="Machinability">machinability</a>. Applications in <a href="/wiki/CdTe_solar_panel" class="mw-redirect" title="CdTe solar panel">CdTe solar panels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cadmium_telluride" title="Cadmium telluride">semiconductors</a> also consume a considerable portion of tellurium production.
</p><p>Tellurium has no biological function, although fungi can use it in place of sulfur and selenium in <a href="/wiki/Amino_acid" title="Amino acid">amino acids</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Cysteine" title="Cysteine">tellurocysteine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Methionine" title="Methionine">telluromethionine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tellurium-fungi_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tellurium-fungi-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In humans, tellurium is partly metabolized into <a href="/wiki/Dimethyl_telluride" title="Dimethyl telluride">dimethyl telluride</a>, (CH<sub>3</sub>)<sub>2</sub>Te, a gas with a <a href="/wiki/Garlic" title="Garlic">garlic</a>-like odor exhaled in the breath of victims of tellurium exposure or poisoning.
</p>
