<a href="/wiki/NFPA_704#Red" title="NFPA 704"><span style="color:black;" title="Flammability code 0: Will not burn. E.g., water">0</span></a></div><div style="width:13px; text-align:center; position:absolute; top:31px; left:15px;">
<a href="/wiki/NFPA_704#Blue" title="NFPA 704"><span style="color:black;" title="Health code 2: Intense or continued but not chronic exposure could cause temporary incapacitation or possible residual injury. E.g., chloroform">2</span></a></div><div style="width:13px; text-align:center; position:absolute; top:31px; left:54px;">
<a href="/wiki/NFPA_704#Yellow" title="NFPA 704"><span style="color:black;" title="Reactivity code 0: Normally stable, even under fire exposure conditions, and is not reactive with water. E.g., liquid nitrogen">0</span></a></div></div></div></div>
</td></tr>




</tbody></table>
<p>Tellurium and tellurium compounds are considered to be mildly <a href="/wiki/Toxic" class="mw-redirect" title="Toxic">toxic</a> and need to be handled with care, although acute poisoning is rare.<sup id="cite_ref-Harrison_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harrison-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Tellurium poisoning is particularly difficult to treat as many <a href="/wiki/Chelating_agents" class="mw-redirect" title="Chelating agents">chelation agents</a> used in the treatment of metal poisoning will increase the toxicity of tellurium. Tellurium is not reported to be carcinogenic.<sup id="cite_ref-Harrison_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harrison-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Humans exposed to as little as 0.01&#160;mg/m<sup>3</sup> or less in air exude a foul <a href="/wiki/Garlic" title="Garlic">garlic</a>-like odor known as "tellurium breath".<sup id="cite_ref-CRC_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CRC-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Distillations_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Distillations-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
This is caused by the body converting tellurium from any oxidation state to <a href="/wiki/Dimethyl_telluride" title="Dimethyl telluride">dimethyl telluride</a>, (CH<sub>3</sub>)<sub>2</sub>Te. This is a volatile compound with a pungent garlic-like smell. Even though the metabolic pathways of tellurium are not known, it is generally assumed that they resemble those of the more extensively studied <a href="/wiki/Selenium" title="Selenium">selenium</a> because the final methylated metabolic products of the two elements are similar.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>People can be exposed to tellurium in the workplace by inhalation, ingestion, skin contact, and eye contact. The <a href="/wiki/Occupational_Safety_and_Health_Administration" title="Occupational Safety and Health Administration">Occupational Safety and Health Administration</a> (OSHA) limits (<a href="/wiki/Permissible_exposure_limit" title="Permissible exposure limit">permissible exposure limit</a>) tellurium exposure in the workplace to 0.1&#160;mg/m<sup>3</sup> over an eight-hour workday. The <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_for_Occupational_Safety_and_Health" title="National Institute for Occupational Safety and Health">National Institute for Occupational Safety and Health</a> (NIOSH) has set the <a href="/wiki/Recommended_exposure_limit" title="Recommended exposure limit">recommended exposure limit</a> (REL) at 0.1&#160;mg/m<sup>3</sup>  over an eight-hour workday. In concentrations of 25&#160;mg/m<sup>3</sup>, tellurium is <a href="/wiki/IDLH" class="mw-redirect" title="IDLH">immediately dangerous to life and health</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tellurium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>The 1862 <a href="/wiki/Telluric_helix" class="mw-redirect" title="Telluric helix">telluric helix</a> of <a href="/wiki/Alexandre-%C3%89mile_B%C3%A9guyer_de_Chancourtois" title="Alexandre-Émile Béguyer de Chancourtois">Alexandre-Émile Béguyer de Chancourtois</a>.</li></ul>
